  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_55521188-d098-4732-9bfc-f5fbc9765ec1'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText16614157451198616764" style="display:none">In this hilarious book, featuring three timeless fables, Dr. Seuss explores the pitfalls of growing too big for your boots!<br /><br />With his unique combination of hilarious stories, zany pictures and riotous rhymes, Dr. Seuss has been delighting young children and helping them learn to read for over fifty years. Creator of the wonderfully anarchic Cat in the Hat, and ranking among the UK’s top ten favourite children’s authors, Seuss is firmly established as a global best-seller, with nearly half a million books sold worldwide.<br /><br />This delightful book forms part of the third stage in HarperCollins’ major Dr. Seuss rebrand programme. With the relaunch of six more titles in January 2004, such all-time favourites as The Lorax, The Foot Book and Yertle the Turtle boast bright new covers that incorporate much needed guidance on reading levels: Blue Back Books are for parents to share with young children, Green Back Books are for budding readers to tackle on their own, and Yellow Back Books are for older, more fluent readers to enjoy. Yertle the Turtle and other stories belongs to the Yellow Back Book range.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1970967672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13477384353745723601"><b>
  <u>A really good titular story!</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>COWABUNGA, DR. SEUSS!</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>And the turtles, of course… all turtles are free.</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>As turtles and, maybe, all creatures should be,</i>
</b><br/><br/>It’s said that Yertle the Turtle exemplifies Hitler, and while I have no doubt of that,...<br/><br/>...I think that he could be King Nimrod (from Tower of Babel’s story) as well, but again,...<br/><br/>...I think that Yertle the Turtle exemplifies all tyrants, cruel to their own people; and fools, wanting to be higher than anybody else.<br/><br/>Yertle the Turtle was</span>
  <span id="freeText13477384353745723601" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>A really good titular story!</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>COWABUNGA, DR. SEUSS!</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>And the turtles, of course… all turtles are free.</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>As turtles and, maybe, all creatures should be,</i>
</b><br /><br />It’s said that Yertle the Turtle exemplifies Hitler, and while I have no doubt of that,...<br /><br />...I think that he could be King Nimrod (from Tower of Babel’s story) as well, but again,...<br /><br />...I think that Yertle the Turtle exemplifies all tyrants, cruel to their own people; and fools, wanting to be higher than anybody else.<br /><br />Yertle the Turtle was king of all that he can see, but that wasn’t enough for him, and started an absurd “tower” made with their fellow turtles, not caring if they weren’t able to sustain such kind of pointless endeavor.<br /><br />An important lesson: Tyrants keep their power as long as their people remain silent.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13477384353745723601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_87798981" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87798981" />
    <a title="Ronyell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell"><img alt="Ronyell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506581787p2/1169488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87798981?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronyell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronyell" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell">Ronyell</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=manners">manners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=picture-book">picture-book</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=my-blog-reviews">my-blog-reviews</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=politics">politics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87798981" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6536023765697408285"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383464521i/6569800.gif' width='400' height='300' alt='Yertle' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I had read many Dr. Seuss books over the years, since I am a huge fan of his work! Now, I had finally come back to one of my childhood favorite stories of all time, “Yertle the Turtle and Other Stories” and I still enjoy it to this very day!<br/><br/>There are a total of three stories in this book which includes “Yertle the Turtle,” “Gertrude McFuzz” and “The Big Brag.”<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Yertle the Turtle</u>
</b><br/><br/>In this tale, Yertle the King of all the Turtles, wanted to have a throne where he could see everything from high abo</span>
  <span id="freeText6536023765697408285" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383464521i/6569800.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="Yertle" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I had read many Dr. Seuss books over the years, since I am a huge fan of his work! Now, I had finally come back to one of my childhood favorite stories of all time, “Yertle the Turtle and Other Stories” and I still enjoy it to this very day!<br><br>There are a total of three stories in this book which includes “Yertle the Turtle,” “Gertrude McFuzz” and “The Big Brag.”<br><br><b>
  <u>Yertle the Turtle</u>
</b><br><br>In this tale, Yertle the King of all the Turtles, wanted to have a throne where he could see everything from high above. So he decided to have the rest of the turtles climb up on each other so he could sit on them to make a throne that would reach up high into the sky. But once Yertle the Turtle became too unbearable, will the other turtles defy him in the end?<br><br><b>
  <u>Gertrude McFuzz</u>
</b><br><br>In this tale, a young bird named Gertrude McFuzz wanted to have a beautiful tail like Lolla-Lee-Lou. So, she decided to visit her uncle Dake and he tells her that in order to grow a beautiful tail like Lolla-Lee-Lou, she has to eat a pill that grows on the pill-berry vine on the top of the hill. But, will Gertrude go too far once she decides to eat all of the pills on the pill-berry vine? <br><br><b>
  <u>The Big Brag</u>
</b><br><br>In this story, a rabbit and a bear were both arguing amongst themselves about who is the best animal in the world and they try to outdo each other with their sense. But when a worm comes by, will he set both the rabbit and the bear straight? <br><br>Dr. Seuss has once again created a truly brilliant and engaging book where each story details the consequences of letting too much pride cloud your good judgment. I enjoyed all of the stories in this book as each story shows a different take on characters becoming too self-absorbed into themselves in certain situations, such as “Yertle the Turtle” showing the consequences of letting the power go to your head, “Gertrude McFuzz” which shows that you should just be yourself and “The Big Brag” which shows that there are better things to do than just bragging. Probably the story I enjoyed the most was “Yertle the Turtle” since I loved the solution to the problem of Yertle making all the other turtles stand on each other to build a throne that can reach the sky (it is a pretty funny solution)! Dr. Seuss’ illustrations are as usual creative and humorous to look at as it is mainly done in black and white colorings with green and blue being the only other colors in this book, which gives the illustrations a distinctive feel. <br><br>Overall, “Yertle the Turtle and Other Stories” is a truly fantastic collection of stories that can be used to teach children about the importance of being humble in your actions and to not become too self-absorbed in yourself. I would recommend this book to children ages four and up since there is nothing inappropriate in this book and the format would be easy for smaller children to understand.<br><br><b>Review is also on: <a href="http://rabbitearsbookblog.blogspot.com/2013/11/yertle-turtle-and-other-stories-by-dr.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabbit Ears Book Blog</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6536023765697408285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1777559" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1777559" />
    <a title="Billy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/92164-billy"><img alt="Billy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1197861019p2/92164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1777559?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Billy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Billy" href="/user/show/92164-billy">Billy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780394800875" href="/book/show/836621.Yertle_the_Turtle_and_Other_Stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/92164-billy?shelf=readalready">readalready</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/92164-billy?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/92164-billy?shelf=politicaltheory">politicaltheory</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1777559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8690692816312404469">This was my favorite book when I was a child. I read it over and over again, memorizing every line, and taking in every lesson about vanity that Dr Seuss was teaching. As an adult I found a whole new appreciation for the book, as I learned that the character of Yertle was based on Adolph Hitler. Seuss used Yertle to demonstrate the rise of fascism in Europe, and show is distaste for it. In the final lines of the story Seuss's true intent comes out as he proclaims that all turtles and every creat</span>
  <span id="freeText8690692816312404469" style="display:none">This was my favorite book when I was a child. I read it over and over again, memorizing every line, and taking in every lesson about vanity that Dr Seuss was teaching. As an adult I found a whole new appreciation for the book, as I learned that the character of Yertle was based on Adolph Hitler. Seuss used Yertle to demonstrate the rise of fascism in Europe, and show is distaste for it. In the final lines of the story Seuss's true intent comes out as he proclaims that all turtles and every creature should be free. <br /><br />That's quite a bit of political theory for a children's book, don't you think? The other two stories have similar themes, mocking competitions of vanity and jealousy. <br /><br />Seuss was no stranger to morals and references to real-world issues. The former political cartoonist took on the Cold War in <i>The Butter Battle Book</i>, Richard Nixon in <i>Marvin K. Mooney Will You Please Go Now!</i>, and the environment in <i>The Lorax</i>. <br /><br />In my opinion Yertle is his best work, and one that I hope lives on with future generations. <br /><br />I spent all this space on Yertle the Turtle and I have yet to mention the "Turtles all the way down" theory of astronomy. Well, that's not really in here, but it sure would be cool if it was. <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8690692816312404469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1897730255513888548" style="display:none">I must've missed this one in my childhood, because I don't remember it at all. I enjoyed it quite a bit, though, even as an adult.<br><br>Even though this book was published decades ago, the themes within the three stories it contains are still fresh and valid. In fact, I think certain politicians should read them (not that it would make much difference; they're as oblivious to their own faults as the rabbit and the bear in "The Big Brag").<br><br>The book is almost 100 pages, but it doesn't feel like it. Each of the stories could be a great bedtime read. The rhyming text would be great fun read aloud.<br><br>Overall, this is a pretty strong trio of stories from Dr. Seuss. For those looking for tales about greed, vanity, and pride, these are some good contenders.<br><br><b>Quotable moment:</b><br><br><blockquote>

  <span id="freeText17558206485145430681" style="display:none">Huzzah! Huzzah! Huzzah!<br /><br />I love it when Dr. Seuss gets preachy.<br /><br />Now, I know my fair share of Dr. Seuss books, but for some reason I'd never heard of Yertle the Turtle until a colleague of mine said I should read it when I teach governments next year.<br /><br />To that colleague: thanks a lot. I just might do that. In fact, I might do that this year as a little review.<br /><br /><br />Yertle is the absolute monarch defined. It's his power becoming absolute and corrupting. It's his greed. It's his fall from the top.<br /><br />He can be happy that the proletariat didn't send him to the guillotine. ...Of course, I'm not sure that <i>that</i> particular method would work for turtles since they would just pull their head back into their shell.<br /><br />Firing squad. Sorry Yertle. If it were up to me, I'd have you sent to<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Hague" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hague</a>.<br /><br />The other stories were fun as well. Vanity and boastfulness - not admirable characteristics according to Mr. Geisel. </span>

The concepts of not making yourself better at the expense of others and the idea that you are not necessarily better than someone else or that you should be happy with who you are are fundamental lessons everyone should take to heart.<br/><br/>Overall, it's an engaging read that really has adult themes while still being appropriate for children.   <span id="freeText712858546453702953" style="display:none">Great stories by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/61105.Dr__Seuss" title="Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">Dr. Seuss</a> that are relevant to adults as well as children. The concepts of not making yourself better at the expense of others and the idea that you are not necessarily better than someone else or that you should be happy with who you are are fundamental lessons everyone should take to heart.<br /><br />Overall, it's an engaging read that really has adult themes while still being appropriate for children. <div id="review_1366759960" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1366759960" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9978483-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524369713p2/9978483.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1366759960?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/9978483-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780394800875" href="/book/show/836621.Yertle_the_Turtle_and_Other_Stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=childrens-book">childrens-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=library-books">library-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9978483-matthew?shelf=dr-seuss">dr-seuss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1366759960" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8057245018500445386">When it comes to short stories, I am not an expert on how to rate the book because sometimes there are stories that you fall in love with the characters and the plot whereas others feel like nails on the chalkboard. I do not have wide range of favorite short stories so you can imagine I was a bit apprehensive when reading this book especially since this is a children's book. Rest to be sure I really enjoyed this book and it feature real-life animals which isn't typical Dr. Seuss to showcase espe</span>
  <span id="freeText8057245018500445386" style="display:none">When it comes to short stories, I am not an expert on how to rate the book because sometimes there are stories that you fall in love with the characters and the plot whereas others feel like nails on the chalkboard. I do not have wide range of favorite short stories so you can imagine I was a bit apprehensive when reading this book especially since this is a children's book. Rest to be sure I really enjoyed this book and it feature real-life animals which isn't typical Dr. Seuss to showcase especially since his imagination has no limits. I will be rating this book by the individual stories.<br /><br /><u>Yertle the Turtle</u>:<b> 5 Stars</b><br /><br />I really loved this story because it showcases the story that people can relate to in real life especially very selfish people. Yertle the Turtle is the King of this miniature pond and he doesn't that theres barely any area to rule as King so he decides to make his throne bigger by stacking turtles on top of each other and for him to sit at the top. When he does that he gets a bigger view of the world around him and definitely wants a bigger view. So he keeps adding turtles without considering others and one of turtles name Mack tells the King that everyone is exhausted and that their shells are bound to crack.<br /><br />Yertle tells him to shut up and obey orders until Mack has enough. He burps and makes the King tumble down where he is now King of the mud while the other turtles laugh at him. For me the message that I discover is that you are not the center of everyones world. If you ask for help do not take advantage of those who are helping you and be thankful with what you have in your life.<br /><br /><u>Gertrude McFuzz</u>:<b> 4.5 Stars</b><br /><br />I enjoyed this short story but the reason why I didn't love it like the others is because the plot is typical and has been used so many times in our history. Gertrude McFuzz is a bird who has one short feather and everything was completely fine until another bird name Lolla-Lee-Lou who has two very long beautiful feathers. Gertrude McFuzz gets jealous and wants to grow longer and more hair to make Lolla jealous. Gertrude succeeds the mission of growing more feathers but the consequence is she became excessive about growing them. <br /><br />She discovered this pill-berry vine and each time you eat a pill, you grow more feathers and longer and unfortunately she took too much of the pill and feather became so long and heavy that she was unable to fly. In the end the other birds help her fly back home where they remove everything except the original feather. I honestly believe that even though each story is different, the messages are extremely similar in terms of being excessive and not knowing your limits.<br /><br /><u>The Big Brag</u>:<b> 5 Stars</b><br /><br />I do not know about this particular book but as I was reading this it gave me this feeling like I was reading an episode of Looney Tunes. I wouldn't be surprise if Dr. Seuss got the inspiration from Looney Tunes because every short story of this book features real life animals. We are introduce to mischievous rabbit who believes he is the best animal in the world (Does that sound familiar?) until a bear comes and challenges him. The rabbit has the ability to hear from far distance but the bear can smell farther than him. <br /><br />Then amongst the battle that was erupting, a worm appeared and told them that he can see farther than both of them and wins. I love the message that no matter how talented or great someone can be there is always someone else who is more talented, stronger, better looking than you. I learn that message early on in my life especially in music and discovered that no matter how talented someone can be there is something unique inside of you that they cannot replicate or beat.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8057245018500445386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_81211544" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81211544" />
    <a title="Dianna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1859681-dianna"><img alt="Dianna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600523642p2/1859681.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81211544?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dianna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dianna" href="/user/show/1859681-dianna">Dianna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81211544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15649813147139531526">This book contains three stories:<br/><br/><i>
  <b>Yertle the Turtle</b>
</i>, a story about a turtle king whose ambitions turn a little too high; <i>
  <b>Gertrude McFuzz</b>
</i>, who is jealous of her friend's tail and gets herself into a mess because of it, and <i>
  <b>The Big Brag</b>
</i>, a story about two animals who argue about who is best, ending with a very wise worm.<br/><br/>---<br/><br/>The message of these stories is to be content with what you are and have—that you are special the way you are and that there's no need to do silly things or to argue </span>
  <span id="freeText15649813147139531526" style="display:none">This book contains three stories:<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Yertle the Turtle</b>
</i>, a story about a turtle king whose ambitions turn a little too high; <i>
  <b>Gertrude McFuzz</b>
</i>, who is jealous of her friend's tail and gets herself into a mess because of it, and <i>
  <b>The Big Brag</b>
</i>, a story about two animals who argue about who is best, ending with a very wise worm.<br /><br />---<br /><br />The message of these stories is to be content with what you are and have—that you are special the way you are and that there's no need to do silly things or to argue about it. <br /><br />The verse! Some of Dr. Seuss's rhyming books are better than others, and I loved this one. The meter is perfect and pleasantly slipped off my tongue as I read it to my son. It wasn't annoyingly hard to read like <i>Fox in Socks</i> and some other books of his; it was a pleasure to read and is perfect for reading out loud. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7979485720736125508">Enjoyed this collection of three stories, the theme this time seems to be about ego.<br/><br/>Yertle is a turtle that is the king of all he sees, one day he realises that if he was higher up he would see more and because of that he would rule over more land. so he makes a throne out of turtles and like all good leaders he abuses those at the bottom.<br/><br/>the next story is about some bird with a rubbish tail and who is jealous of another bird who has a pretty tail. so she hatches a plan to get a better tail with</span>
  <span id="freeText7979485720736125508" style="display:none">Enjoyed this collection of three stories, the theme this time seems to be about ego.<br /><br />Yertle is a turtle that is the king of all he sees, one day he realises that if he was higher up he would see more and because of that he would rule over more land. so he makes a throne out of turtles and like all good leaders he abuses those at the bottom.<br /><br />the next story is about some bird with a rubbish tail and who is jealous of another bird who has a pretty tail. so she hatches a plan to get a better tail with disastrous consequences.<br /><br />The final story is a rabbit and a bear fighting each over bragging rights for who is the best, little do they know that I am in fact the best.<br /><br />Good fun stuff and another Dr Seuss book crossed off the list as read.</span>

<div id="review_1473175201" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1473175201" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1473175201?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780394800875" href="/book/show/836621.Yertle_the_Turtle_and_Other_Stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1473175201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2926074595790931043"><em>Yertle the Turtle and Other Stories</em> is targeted for older, more fluent young readers.<br/><br/>You know that I do enjoy reading books aimed at readers younger than myself…and every year those numbers keep getting bigger and bigger. Hmmm, I do feel a bit Seuss-y, so perhaps I should say, those numbers are humongouser and humongouser?<br/><br/>Reading Dr. Seuss is actually research on my part, as I have finally set my sights on writing the children's book I've had in mind. And…my sentences need some work. *Stop laugh</span>
  <span id="freeText2926074595790931043" style="display:none"><em>Yertle the Turtle and Other Stories</em> is targeted for older, more fluent young readers.<br /><br />You know that I do enjoy reading books aimed at readers younger than myself…and every year those numbers keep getting bigger and bigger. Hmmm, I do feel a bit Seuss-y, so perhaps I should say, those numbers are humongouser and humongouser?<br /><br />Reading Dr. Seuss is actually research on my part, as I have finally set my sights on writing the children's book I've had in mind. And…my sentences need some work. *Stop laughing!* Even better, I've always meant to sit down with Dr. Seuss and get caught up on what I missed in my childhood.<br /><br />I do like the inside of the cover, lol, it's a green sea of turtles, each with their own textured backs. Each with their own style of hair as they ride the waves.<br /><br /><b>The Stories</b><br />"<strong>Yertle the Turtle</strong>" is a cautionary tale about aiming too high, especially on the backs of others…as Mack can attest. As for the rhyming…I'm in love, and I also know I'll never be able to match Seuss in that!<br /><br />"<strong>Gertrude McFuzz</strong>" is a much more palatable, for us anyway, story of being careful what you wish for, as poor Gertrude McFuzz learned to her dismay.<br /><br />I must say the rhyming in this was more awkward, although I did fall into the swing of it. I could definitely imagine myself sing-songing along.<br /><br />"<strong>The Big Brag</strong>" is won by the least of them all, as he shows up two braggarts for being so ridiculous. Again, the rhyme has its rough spots, but I do adore Dr. Seuss' storytelling techniques for getting another moral tale across with laughter.<br /><br /><b>The Cover and Title</b><br />The cover is a grass green background with a white cloud and the title and author's name in white. There are five blue-backed turtles perched precariously atop one another — it's only the top one, Yertle the Turtle King, who looks happy about his position.<br /><br />The title leads with the best of them all with a grandiose turtle to the lowliest worm with <em>Yertle the Turtle and Other Stories</em>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2926074595790931043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_687990619" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/687990619" />
    <a title="Matthew Hunter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3040804-matthew-hunter"><img alt="Matthew Hunter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495642903p2/3040804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/687990619?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Hunter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Hunter" href="/user/show/3040804-matthew-hunter">Matthew Hunter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3040804-matthew-hunter?shelf=children-picture-books">children-picture-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer687990619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11435335917934016689">Dr. Seuss the revolutionary! Man <i>Yertle the Turtle</i>'s some good stuff. I'll let the master tell his own story beginning from the point where Yertle threatens to stack thousands of turtles one on top of the other so that, from atop the stack, he can become king of everything he surveys:<br/><blockquote>But, as Yertle, the Turtle King, lifted his hand<br/>And started to order and give the command,<br/>That plain little turtle below in the stack,<br/>That plain little turtle whose name was just Mack,<br/>Decided he’d taken enough. And </blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText11435335917934016689" style="display:none">Dr. Seuss the revolutionary! Man <i>Yertle the Turtle</i>'s some good stuff. I'll let the master tell his own story beginning from the point where Yertle threatens to stack thousands of turtles one on top of the other so that, from atop the stack, he can become king of everything he surveys:<br /><blockquote>But, as Yertle, the Turtle King, lifted his hand<br />And started to order and give the command,<br />That plain little turtle below in the stack,<br />That plain little turtle whose name was just Mack,<br />Decided he’d taken enough. And he had.<br />And that plain little lad got a bit mad.<br />And that plain little Mack did a plain little thing.<br />He burped!<br />And his burp shook the throne of the king!<br /><br />And Yertle the Turtle, the king of the trees,<br />The king of the air and the birds and the bees,<br />The king of a house and a cow and a mule…<br />Well, that was the end of the Turtle King’s rule!<br />For Yertle, the King of all Sala-ma-Sond,<br />Fell off his high throne and fell Plunk! in the pond!<br /><br />And today the great Yertle, that Marvelous he,<br />Is King of the Mud. That is all he can see.<br />And the turtles, of course… all the turtles are free<br />As turtles and, maybe, all creatures should be.</blockquote><br />A king's tyrannical actions lead to stress-induced indigestion and angst among the lowest on the societal totem pole. And poof! The king topples from his throne. Dr. Seuss has given us a catchily-rhymed parable about the power of democracy from below. And I wasn't the only one who liked it. Unlike our bedtime read of the too-long <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7781.The_500_Hats_of_Bartholomew_Cubbins" title="The 500 Hats of Bartholomew Cubbins by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">The 500 Hats of Bartholomew Cubbins</a> which touched on similar themes, Sigourney asked for numerous repeat tellings of <i>Yertle</i>. It's a good picture book that appeals to adults (well, this adult) and children alike. An easy five star rating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11435335917934016689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8009748?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Sammis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Sammis" href="/user/show/122647-sarah-sammis">Sarah Sammis</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122647-sarah-sammis?shelf=read-as-a-child">read-as-a-child</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122647-sarah-sammis?shelf=read-to-me">read-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122647-sarah-sammis?shelf=pc">pc</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8009748" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3257275435699240297">Yertle the Turtle and Other Stories has three short stories, one against fascism, one against jealousy and one against bragging. The two my kids enjoy reading most are the first and third, "Yertle the Turtle" and "The Big Brag."<br/><br/>Back when Theodor Geisel was working as a political cartoonist, he drew an anti Hitler cartoon showing a stack of turtles in a V-shape. The caption said "You can't build a substantial V out of turtles!" You can see it reproduced in Dr. Seuss Goes to War by by Richard H. M</span>
  <span id="freeText3257275435699240297" style="display:none">Yertle the Turtle and Other Stories has three short stories, one against fascism, one against jealousy and one against bragging. The two my kids enjoy reading most are the first and third, "Yertle the Turtle" and "The Big Brag."<br /><br />Back when Theodor Geisel was working as a political cartoonist, he drew an anti Hitler cartoon showing a stack of turtles in a V-shape. The caption said "You can't build a substantial V out of turtles!" You can see it reproduced in Dr. Seuss Goes to War by by Richard H. Minear.<br /><br />Yertle, the despot king turtle, decides he wants to increase his kingdom. Turtle law says he's the king of all he can see. To increase his view and thus his kingdom, he stands on the backs of his turtle subjects. His own lust for power ends up being his literal downfall.<br /><br />The second story, "Gertrude McFuzz" is about a bird who is jealous of another bird with a more beautiful tail. She goes to great lengths to increase the beauty of her tail but loses the ability to fly in the process. She has to learn to be happy with who she is the way she is.<br /><br />The final story is "The Big Brag" which reminds me of Sean and his best friend. They love to brag to each other about all the great things they have or all the great things they can do. Their bragging will often times come in the way of actually playing until they are called on it. In this story the bragging pair are rabbit and a bear. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3257275435699240297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12617909733113155805">Lisa Simpson once seriously - but hilariously - said, "And please don't deprive yourselves of wonderful books like ... 'Yertle the Turtle' -- possibly the best book ever written on the subject of turtle stacking." Ever since I saw that episode, years ago, I've wanted to read Yertle the Turtle, not so much for the sake of reading it, but to better appreciate the Simpsons joke. Well, I just read the book, and indeed my appreciation for the joke has increased. <br/><br/>It's a cute story about a turtle, king</span>
  <span id="freeText12617909733113155805" style="display:none">Lisa Simpson once seriously - but hilariously - said, "And please don't deprive yourselves of wonderful books like ... 'Yertle the Turtle' -- possibly the best book ever written on the subject of turtle stacking." Ever since I saw that episode, years ago, I've wanted to read Yertle the Turtle, not so much for the sake of reading it, but to better appreciate the Simpsons joke. Well, I just read the book, and indeed my appreciation for the joke has increased. <br /><br />It's a cute story about a turtle, king of a pond, who commands other turtles to stack themselves up so that he can sit upon them as he might a throne and look far and wild upon everything he can see, which he also happens to believe is everything under his rule.<br /><br />I read this at age 25, and liked it, thought it cute with a good lesson. I'm sure if I read this book at age 5, what with 20 years of nostalgia, I'd rank it a 5. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13851919504330171465">This book was alright. Of course Dr. Seuss is known for putting political morals inside pretty much all of his books, so I think that it was easier to read because it wasn't completely toned down for young readers. I enjoyed "Yertle the Turtle" out of the other stories because at the end when Yertle the King was no longer king, it showed Mack (the one who kicked the king off his throne) on the rock showing that he may get greedy and make another throne out of helpless turtles. There is a lot bet</span>
  <span id="freeText13851919504330171465" style="display:none">This book was alright. Of course Dr. Seuss is known for putting political morals inside pretty much all of his books, so I think that it was easier to read because it wasn't completely toned down for young readers. I enjoyed "Yertle the Turtle" out of the other stories because at the end when Yertle the King was no longer king, it showed Mack (the one who kicked the king off his throne) on the rock showing that he may get greedy and make another throne out of helpless turtles. There is a lot between the lines that don't jump out to you, but if you carefully analyze his works you'll see the relation to political morals.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iI+TJ2aUzLqMccmHankiRl5JQRH0HwbkCSjy6WGmjJ+aCx5qCaF+RXY0wfndQXH8PS36DvMcdaA+R8GHz5funA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('J/yf939ihddVye0plJwGsejptZH9tw5HtHhLCz6hXcA1eBK6EFc3KK+M5VcjpFULi40Ojvq0fQODF3hlkJA/ww==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/61105.Dr_Seuss">About Dr. Seuss</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/61105.Dr_Seuss"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1193930952p3/61105.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/61105.Dr_Seuss">Dr. Seuss
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
16,563
followers
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1653981493167821153">Theodor Seuss Geisel was born 2 March 1904 in Springfield, MA. He graduated Dartmouth College in 1925, and proceeded on to Oxford University with the intent of acquiring a doctorate in literature. At Oxford he met Helen Palmer, who he wed in 1927. He returned from Europe in 1927, and began working for a magazine called Judge, the leading humor magazine in America at the time, submitting both carto</span>
  <span id="freeText1653981493167821153" style="display:none">Theodor Seuss Geisel was born 2 March 1904 in Springfield, MA. He graduated Dartmouth College in 1925, and proceeded on to Oxford University with the intent of acquiring a doctorate in literature. At Oxford he met Helen Palmer, who he wed in 1927. He returned from Europe in 1927, and began working for a magazine called Judge, the leading humor magazine in America at the time, submitting both cartoons and humorous articles for them. Additionally, he was submitting cartoons to Life, Vanity Fair and Liberty. In some of his works, he'd made reference to an insecticide called Flit. These references gained notice, and led to a contract to draw comic ads for Flit. This association lasted 17 years, gained him national exposure, and coined the catchphrase "Quick, Henry, the Flit!" <br /><br />In 1936 on the way to a vaction in Europe, listening to the rhythm of the ship's engines, he came up with And to Think That I Saw It on Mulberry Street, which was then promptly rejected by the first 43 publishers he showed it to. Eventually in 1937 a friend published the book for him, and it went on to at least moderate success. <br /><br />During WW II, Geisel joined the army and was sent to Hollywood. Captain Geisel would write for Frank Capra's Signal Corps Unit (for which he won the Legion of Merit) and do documentaries (he won Oscar's for Hitler Lives and Design for Death). He also created a cartoon called Gerald McBoing-Boing which also won him an Oscar. <br /><br />In May of 1954, Life published a report concerning illiteracy among school children. The report said, among other things, that children were having trouble to read because their books were boring. This inspired Geisel's publisher, and prompted him to send Geisel a list of 400 words he felt were important, asked him to cut the list to 250 words (the publishers idea of how many words at one time a first grader could absorb), and write a book. Nine months later, Geisel, using 220 of the words given to him published The Cat in the Hat, which went on to instant success. <br /><br />In 1960 Bennett Cerf bet Geisel $50 that he couldn't write an entire book using only fifty words. The result was Green Eggs and Ham. Cerf never paid the $50 from the bet. <br /><br />Helen Palmer Geisel died in 1967. Theodor Geisel married Audrey Stone Diamond in 1968. Theodor Seuss Geisel died 24 September 1991. <br /><br />Also worked under the pen name:<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/398177.Theo_Le_Sieg" rel="nofollow noopener">Theo Le Sieg</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="1653981493167821153" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
